2025-02-10T16:10:46.9955199Z             ``seek()`` and ``read()`` methods and must always

2025-02-10T16:10:46.9956295Z             file-like object support the ``readline()`` method as well.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9956818Z         mmap_mode : {None, 'r+', 'r', 'w+', 'c'}, optional
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9957361Z             If not None, then memory-map the file, using the given mode (see
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9957977Z             `numpy.memmap` for a detailed description of the modes).  A
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9958597Z             memory-mapped array is kept on disk. However, it can be accessed
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9959253Z             and sliced like any ndarray.  Memory mapping is especially useful
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9959898Z             for accessing small fragments of large files without reading the
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9960410Z             entire file into memory.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9960790Z         allow_pickle : bool, optional
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9961286Z             Allow loading pickled object arrays stored in npy files. Reasons for
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9961889Z             disallowing pickles include security, as loading pickled data can
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9962460Z             execute arbitrary code. If pickles are disallowed, loading object
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9962964Z             arrays will fail. Default: False
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9963290Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9964330Z             .. versionchanged:: 1.16.3
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9964765Z                 Made default False in response to CVE-2019-6446.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9965165Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9965648Z         fix_imports : bool, optional
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9966165Z             Only useful when loading Python 2 generated pickled files on Python 3,
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9966832Z             which includes npy/npz files containing object arrays. If `fix_imports`
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9967567Z             is True, pickle will try to map the old Python 2 names to the new names
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9968090Z             used in Python 3.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9968475Z         encoding : str, optional
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9968998Z             What encoding to use when reading Python 2 strings. Only useful when
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9969644Z             loading Python 2 generated pickled files in Python 3, which includes
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9970299Z             npy/npz files containing object arrays. Values other than 'latin1',
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9970933Z             'ASCII', and 'bytes' are not allowed, as they can corrupt numerical
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9971426Z             data. Default: 'ASCII'
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9971795Z         max_header_size : int, optional
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9972272Z             Maximum allowed size of the header.  Large headers may not be safe
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9972899Z             to load securely and thus require explicitly passing a larger value.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9973447Z             See :py:func:`ast.literal_eval()` for details.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9974186Z             This option is ignored when `allow_pickle` is passed.  In that case
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9974771Z             the file is by definition trusted and the limit is unnecessary.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9975217Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9975434Z         Returns
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9975693Z         -------
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9975979Z         result : array, tuple, dict, etc.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9976456Z             Data stored in the file. For ``.npz`` files, the returned instance
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9977080Z             of NpzFile class must be closed to avoid leaking file descriptors.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9977536Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9977759Z         Raises
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9978000Z         ------
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9978235Z         OSError
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9978546Z             If the input file does not exist or cannot be read.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9978951Z         UnpicklingError
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9979351Z             If ``allow_pickle=True``, but the file cannot be loaded as a pickle.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9979803Z         ValueError
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9980192Z             The file contains an object array, but ``allow_pickle=False`` given.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9980673Z         EOFError
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9981055Z             When calling ``np.load`` multiple times on the same file handle,
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9981535Z             if all data has already been read
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9981888Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9982108Z         See Also
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9982362Z         --------
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9982653Z         save, savez, savez_compressed, loadtxt
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9983158Z         memmap : Create a memory-map to an array stored in a file on disk.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9983928Z         lib.format.open_memmap : Create or load a memory-mapped ``.npy`` file.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9984420Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9984619Z         Notes
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9984850Z         -----
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9985198Z         - If the file contains pickle data, then whatever object is stored
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9985664Z           in the pickle is returned.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9986085Z         - If the file is a ``.npy`` file, then a single array is returned.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9986625Z         - If the file is a ``.npz`` file, then a dictionary-like object is
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9987207Z           returned, containing ``{filename: array}`` key-value pairs, one for
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9987711Z           each file in the archive.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9988426Z         - If the file is a ``.npz`` file, the returned value supports the
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9989058Z           context manager protocol in a similar fashion to the open function::
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9989719Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9989969Z             with load('foo.npz') as data:
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9990312Z                 a = data['a']
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9990601Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9990969Z           The underlying file descriptor is closed when exiting the 'with'
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9991422Z           block.
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9991668Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9991887Z         Examples
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9992134Z         --------
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9992424Z         Store data to disk, and load it again:
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9992769Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9993056Z         >>> np.save('/tmp/123', np.array([[1, 2, 3], [4, 5, 6]]))
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9993482Z         >>> np.load('/tmp/123.npy')
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9994002Z         array([[1, 2, 3],
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9994303Z                [4, 5, 6]])
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9994580Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9994871Z         Store compressed data to disk, and load it again:
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9995264Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9995504Z         >>> a=np.array([[1, 2, 3], [4, 5, 6]])
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9995844Z         >>> b=np.array([1, 2])
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9996180Z         >>> np.savez('/tmp/123.npz', a=a, b=b)
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9996552Z         >>> data = np.load('/tmp/123.npz')
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9996891Z         >>> data['a']
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9997155Z         array([[1, 2, 3],
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9997422Z                [4, 5, 6]])
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9997702Z         >>> data['b']
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9997952Z         array([1, 2])
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9998228Z         >>> data.close()
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9998491Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9998810Z         Mem-map the stored array, and then access the second row
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9999242Z         directly from disk:
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9999528Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:46.9999791Z         >>> X = np.load('/tmp/123.npy', mmap_mode='r')
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0000151Z         >>> X[1, :]
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0000408Z         memmap([4, 5, 6])
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0000689Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0000910Z         """
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0001211Z         if encoding not in ('ASCII', 'latin1', 'bytes'):
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0001722Z             # The 'encoding' value for pickle also affects what encoding
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0002239Z             # the serialized binary data of NumPy arrays is loaded
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0002744Z             # in. Pickle does not pass on the encoding information to
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0003256Z             # NumPy. The unpickling code in numpy.core.multiarray is
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0004043Z             # written to assume that unicode data appearing where binary
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0004623Z             # should be is in 'latin1'. 'bytes' is also safe, as is 'ASCII'.
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0005064Z             #
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0005446Z             # Other encoding values can corrupt binary data, and we
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0006044Z             # purposefully disallow them. For the same reason, the errors=
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0006616Z             # argument is not exposed, as values other than 'strict'
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0007137Z             # result can similarly silently corrupt numerical data.
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0007717Z             raise ValueError("encoding must be 'ASCII', 'latin1', or 'bytes'")
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0008191Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0008559Z         pickle_kwargs = dict(encoding=encoding, fix_imports=fix_imports)
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0009021Z     
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0009289Z         with contextlib.ExitStack() as stack:
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0009679Z             if hasattr(file, 'read'):
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0010012Z                 fid = file
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0010316Z                 own_fid = False
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0010620Z             else:
2025-02-10T16:10:47.0010982Z >               fid = stack.enter_context(open(os_fspath(file), "rb"))
